# Comments for Question 4, LLM=Amazon Nova Pro

== Grader: Claude 3.7 Sonnet ==
  * grade_story_104.txt (grade=4.5)
    The story relies heavily on telling rather than showing, particularly regarding the steward's emotional state. The symbolism of the cameo as rebellion feels imposed rather than emerging naturally. The central theme of conformity versus individuality is explicitly stated rather than subtly explored. The ending lacks impact because the stakes and specific consequences of the steward's actions remain unclear.

  * grade_story_0.txt (grade=5.8)

The lamp serves as effective symbolism, but other literary devices are sparse. The central conflict—taming the monster—is clear, but lacks sufficient tension. The theme of unity and forgotten promises emerges, but the story doesn't push beyond surface-level exploration to create deeper resonance or provoke substantial reflection.

The metaphors (particularly the quilt and stamps) remain surface-level without developing deeper significance.

  * grade_story_100.txt (grade=3.6)

  * grade_story_10.txt (grade=6.5)
    Uses metaphor (recipes as flaws) and symbolism (metamorphosis) creatively, but emotional resonance is undercut by abstraction. Ending feels tidy rather than earned, limiting thematic impact. Subtextual links are present but underdeveloped.

  * grade_story_1.txt (grade=5.0)
    Themes of fear/confrontation are explicit but shallow; symbolic gestures (e.g., unraveling knots) feel trite rather than resonant.

  * grade_story_0.txt (grade=7.8)
    Symbolism (lamp, promises) and subtext about forgotten unity resonate, but emotional impact remains surface-level; the ending resolves effectively but lacks lingering resonance or layered meaning.

  * grade_story_101.txt (grade=5.8)
    Generic symbolism and abstract themes; emotional resonance is shallow, ending feels summative rather than impactful.

  * grade_story_107.txt (grade=5.0)

  * grade_story_102.txt (grade=5.8)

  * grade_story_108.txt (grade=6.4)

  * grade_story_105.txt (grade=3.8)
